Stilp v. Cappy


No. 647 M.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


931 A.2d 108; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 469


July 20, 2007, Submitted  
August 15, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Stilp v. Commonwealth, 588 Pa. 539, 905 A.2d 918, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 1736 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to 42 Pa.C.S. § 761, petitioner citizen sued respondents, the Chief Justice of the Pennsylvania Supreme Court, the Court Administrator of Pennsylvania, and Pennsylvania's Acting Treasurer, challenging the legality of annual cost of living adjustments (COLAs) for all Pennsylvania judges and seeking a writ of mandamus. Respondents filed preliminary objections to the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court had previously held that the legislature's repeal by Act 72 of Act 44 was unconstitutional insofar as it reduced judicial compensation; enjoined the repeal of Act 44 in part; and ordered that judicial compensation be calculated under Act 44. Petitioner filed the instant suit, arguing that as the supreme court did not address the issue of whether the judges would be entitled to COLAs under Act 44 or former 42 Pa.C.S. § 1810, respondents had no authority to grant COLAs to judges. The trial court initially held that it had subject matter jurisdiction over this suit under 42 Pa.C.S. § 761, because it was a civil action filed against state officers. But as the supreme court, not the Chief Justice, had authority over the Administrative Office of Pennsylvania Courts, the Chief Justice was not a proper party to the action. As to the merits of petitioner's claim, Pennsylvania judges were clearly entitled to COLAs under 65 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 366.2a(i); therefore, the fact that the supreme court had not reinstated 42 Pa.C.S. § 1810 was immaterial. Thus, the complaint did not state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The trial court sustained the preliminary objection which contended that the complaint failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted and dismissed with the complaint with prejudice.

Pilchesky v. Rendell

COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


932 A.2d 287; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 464

Decision reached on appeal by Pilchesky v. Rendell, 596 Pa. 473, 946 A.2d 92, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 573 (2008)
Related proceeding at Pilchesky v. Rendell, 2011 Pa. Commw. Unpub. LEXIS 642 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.
Vutnoski v. Redevelopment Auth., 907 A.2d 682, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 525 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an amended petition for review seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, to which respondents, government officials and others, filed preliminary objections. The matter involved the transfer of a 10-acre complex--a dedicated public park, which was purchased in 1977 with "Project 70" funds and carried restrictions as to its use--from a city redevelopment authority to a city university.


OVERVIEW: The amended petition raised constitutional challenges to the passage of the act that transferred the complex. The court concluded that the pleaded facts were insufficient to state a claim against the governor because petitioner cited to no legal authority for the proposition that a governor had a duty to make inquires before signing legislation. In addition, the House of Representatives and its members were immune from suit under the Speech and Debate Clause, Pa. Const. art. 2, § 15, because all these parties did was participate in the legislative process. This same reasoning applied to the Senate parties. 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 3946.20(b) provided limitations on the alienation of property acquired under the Project 70 Land Acquisition and Borrowing Act, 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 3946.1-3946.22, by directing that owners of such property could not dispose of the land without the approval of the General Assembly. Because the General Assembly acted under its constitutional authority in adopting the Project 70 Act, and acted pursuant to its authority under the Act in approving the transfer of the property, the amended petition failed to state a claim against the Senate.


OUTCOME: The preliminary objections of the governor, the House of Representatives, the Speaker of the House, the Majority Leader of the House, the Senate, the Minority Leader of the Senate, and the President Pro Tempore of the Senate, were sustained. The remaining claims were transferred to the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania).

Piunti v. DOL & Indus., Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review


No. 482 M.D. 2005


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


933 A.2d 135; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 583; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P12,519


November 15, 2006, Argued 
August 9, 2007, Decided 
August 9, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Publication Ordered October 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Piunti v. DOL & Indus., Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review, 900 A.2d 1017, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 320 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys filed an amended petition for review, alleging that the adoption of 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 774 violated Pa. Const. art. V, § 10 by allowing non-employee, non-attorneys to represent corporate employers in unemployment proceedings. The attorneys also filed a motion for summary judgment. Respondent, the Pennsylvania Department of Labor and Industry, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, filed a motion for summary relief.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court concluded that the adoption of 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 774 did not violate Pa. Const. art. V, § 10 because the state supreme court had opined that non-employee, non-lawyers representing parties in unemployment compensation proceedings were not practicing law. Thus, the attorneys were clearly not entitled to summary judgment on their claim. With respect to the Board's motion for summary relief, the appellate court agreed that, while the state supreme court's plurality decision in Harkness II was not precedential, its reasoning was still highly persuasive. In reversing the appellate court's decision in Harkness I that a non-employee, non-attorney could not represent an employer at an unemployment compensation hearing, the state supreme court had removed the underlying support for the attorneys' claim that 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 774 was unconstitutional. Thus, the Board was entitled to judgment on the attorneys' claim as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The attorneys' motion for summary judgment was denied, and the Board's motion for summary relief was granted.

Ins. Fed'n of Pa., Inc. v. Ins. Dep't


No. 10 M.D. 2004


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


929 A.2d 1243; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 403


April 11, 2007, Argued 
July 26, 2007, Decided 
July 26, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Ins. Fedn. of Pa., Inc. v. Commonwealth, 2009 Pa. LEXIS 1037 (Pa., May 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ins. Fed'n of Pa., Inc. v. Ins. Dep't, 586 Pa. 268, 893 A.2d 69, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 19 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Insurers filed a petition for review requesting a declaration that a notice published by the Insurance Department explaining the Department's interpretation of statutes relating to insurance coverage for drug and alcohol dependency treatment and regulation of managed health care was inconsistent with the statutes. The parties moved for judgment on the pleadings. Following a remand, the court considered the merits.


OVERVIEW: The statutes were known as Act 106, 40 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 908-1 to 908-8, and Act 68, 40 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 991.2101 to 991.2194. The Department's notice stated that under Act 106, the only lawful prerequisite before an insured obtains nonhospital residential and outpatient coverage for alcohol and drug dependency treatment was a certification and referral from a licensed physician or licensed psychologist. The Department determined that Act 68 did not change the requirements under Act 106 and should be read in conjunction with the existing requirements. The insurers argued that no language in Act 106 stripped managed care plans of their ability to perform medical necessity and utilization review with respect to these benefits. The court held that the Department's view of the issue was the most logical and rational one, more in keeping with the intent of the legislature and the rules of statutory construction. The court held that Act 106 plainly provided for mandatory benefits and that nothing solely on its face, apart from certification and referral, limited the availability of mandatory benefits by any extraneous procedures.


OUTCOME: The motion for judgment on the pleadings filed by the Insurance Department was granted, and the petition for review in this matter was dismissed with prejudice.

 

1845 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Stilp v. Commonwealth


No. 572 M.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


927 A.2d 707; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 338


April 13, 2007, Submitted 
July 3, 2007, Decided 
July 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Stilp v. Gen. Assembly, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 223 (Pa., Mar. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner resident taxpayer challenged an amendment to County Code, art. XIV, 16 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 1401-1441, known as Act 57 of 2005, Act 57 of 2005, 2005 Pa. Laws 312, which allowed sitting district attorneys to convert from part-time to full-time status, with an accompanying increase in compensation. Respondents, the general assembly and the presiding officer of each house, filed preliminary objections.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer alleged that Act 57 violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 27. Respondents sought dismissal of the suit on either of two bases: legislative immunity pursuant to Pa. Const. art. II, § 15 or the taxpayer's lack of standing because the amendment did not impact the district attorney in the county where the taxpayer lived. In sustaining the preliminary objections, the court found that the taxpayer lacked standing. The taxpayer did not contend that Act 57 caused any discernible adverse effect to any of his interests other than the abstract interest of all citizens in having others comply with the law. Thus, it was clear that the taxpayer did not enjoy standing under the traditional test. The taxpayer lacked taxpayer standing because he was not the best situated to assert a challenge to Act 57. County commissioners, controllers, auditors or treasurers in any of the 31 counties in which the status of the district attorney changed after Act 57 would be the best suited to challenge the statute because county finances under their control would be detrimentally affected by the county's share of increased compensation to be paid to another county officer, the district attorney.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the preliminary objection to standing and dismissed the suit.

Reed v. Harrisburg City Council


Nos. 406 & 783 C.D. 2007


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


927 A.2d 698; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 339


June 13, 2007, Argued 
July 2, 2007, Decided 
July 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Reed v. Harrisburg City Council, 593 Pa. 419, 931 A.2d 629, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1742 (2007)
Decision reached on appeal by Reed v. Harrisburg City Council, 2010 Pa. LEXIS 1129 (Pa., May 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 2007-CV-1761-EQ. Common Pleas Court of the County of Dauphin. Kleinfelter, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Harrisburg City Council sought review of the orders of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Dauphin (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee mayor a preliminary injunction against the enforcement of Harrisburg, Pa., Ordinance 36-2006 (January 23, 2007) (the Ordinance) and prohibited the Council's appointees to the Harrisburg Authority Board from acting as members of the Board.


OVERVIEW: The Council appointed Board members, pursuant to an Ordinance passed over the mayor's veto. The court dissolved the preliminary injunction prohibiting the Council from enforcing its Ordinance and its appointees from acting as Board members. The court held that the trial court arguably had reasonable grounds, pursuant to 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 41608(b) of the Third Class City Charter Law, to enjoin the Council from seating appointees before the Ordinance's March 12, 2007, effective date; however, the trial court had no apparently reasonable grounds to enjoin the City from enforcing its Ordinance. The court held that the mayor failed to satisfy the essential prerequisites to an injunction because there was no actual proof of irreparable harm from the appointments to the operations of the Board, the fiscal issues, the Board's bonds or bondholders, or the completion of an incinerator project. The court held that the trial court recognized that it was not clear whether the Ordinance violated any enabling statutes or whether the mayor had a right to relief and did not discuss the Municipality Authorities Act, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 5601-5623, or statutes defining the term "governing body."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders and dissolved the preliminary injunction.

Mazur v. Trinity Area Sch. Dist.


No. 824 C.D. 2006, No. 829 C.D. 2006, No. 825 C.D. 2006, No. 826 C.D. 2006, No. 827 C.D. 2006, No. 828 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


926 A.2d 1260; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 324


February 7, 2007, Argued 
June 25, 2007, Decided 
June 25, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part, Appeal denied by, in part Mazur v. Trinity Area Sch. Dist., 596 Pa. 206, 941 A.2d 1256, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 8 (2008)
Affirmed by Mazur v. Trinity Area Sch. Dist., 2008 Pa. LEXIS 2315 (Pa., Dec. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 2005-6321. Common Pleas Court of the County of Washington. Terputac, Senior Judge.
Mazur v. Wash. County Redevelopment Auth., 900 A.2d 1024, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 324 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An unincorporated association and others filed actions against local taxing districts and others challenging the use of tax increment financing for a commercial development project. The Washington County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) sustained the preliminary objections of the taxing districts to the six consolidated actions. The association appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The taxing districts approved the use of tax increment financing for a proposes 333-acre commercial development. On appeal, the association first argued that the trial court erred in holding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The appellate court held that an appeal would not lie under the Local Agency Law, 2 Pa.C.S. §§ 551-555, 751-754, from the enactment of a resolution by a local taxing entity authorizing the use of tax increment financing for a commercial development. The appellate court found that the association's conclusory allegations in their claims for equitable relief were nothing more than an attack on the wisdom of the legislative enactments. The appellate court further held that the trial court properly sustained the districts' demurrer to a claim that the districts acted in bad faith in determining that the area of the development was blighted. The association's argument that because township supervisors voted to rezone the property to a commercial designation, the districts could not in good faith have believed the property to be blighted was a bald assertion, unsupported by any clear averments of fact to support a finding of fraud or bad faith.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


 

1848 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Mitchell's Bar & Rest., Inc. v. Allegheny County


No. 191 C.D. 2007, No. 192 C.D. 2007


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


924 A.2d 730; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 247


March 6, 2007, Argued  
May 22, 2007, Decided  
May 22, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. GD 06-29159. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Vecchia, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two restaurants, sought review of a decision of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny (Pennsylvania), which found that the Commonwealth's Clean Indoor Air Act, which regulated indoor smoking in public places, was not ultra vires. It also denied permanent injunctive relief, although it granted an injunction to prevent enforcement of the ordinance. At issue were §§ 10.1 and 15.1 of the Act of April 27, 1927, Pub. L. No. 465.


OVERVIEW: The Act broadly applied to municipalities, and § 15.1 of the Act specified that the Act preempted and superseded any local ordinance or rule concerning the subject matter of § 10.1 of the Act, 35 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 1235.1(a). Section 10.1 regulated smoking in restaurants. The county, however, adopted an ordinance that prohibited all smoking in public places. Preliminarily, the state commonwealth court found that § 15.1 of the Act had not been repealed. Although the Pennsylvania Construction Code Act of November 10, 1999, Pub. L. No. 491, as amended, 35 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 7210.101-7210.1103, included a provision that, when effective, would repeal § 15.1, the repealing regulations were not published for a number of years, and, in the interim the repealer was repealed. Because the repealer never went into effect, the status quo continued, and § 15.1 of the Act was not affected. Accordingly, the county was without authority to enact the ordinance based upon the express preemption language contained in § 15.1. Moreover, as the trial court erred in concluding that the ordinance was not ultra vires, it erred by not enjoining the county from seeking to enforce it.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying declaratory judgment in favor of the restaurants was reversed, as was its order denying their request for permanent injunctive relief. The case was remanded to the trial court with the direction that it enter a permanent injunction against the county with regard to the enforcement of its anti-smoking ordinance.

Cutler v. State Civil Serv. Comm'n


No. 2178 C.D. 2005


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


924 A.2d 706; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 365


April 9, 2007, Argued 
May 17, 2007, Decided 
May 17, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Cutler v. State Civ. Serv. Comm'n (Office of Admin.), 940 A.2d 366, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2838 (Pa., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 24384. State Civil Service Commission.
Cutler v. State Civ. Serv. Comm'n, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 500 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Sept. 20, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of the adjudication of respondent, the State Civil Service Commission, which sustained the decision of the Office of Administration not to appoint him to the position of Pennsylvania Management Associate (PMA). The employee was offered, and he had accepted, the PMA position. However, upon removal of a 10 point veterans' preference, the PMA offer was withdrawn.


OVERVIEW: The Commission held that the employee, a veteran, was not entitled to have 10 points added to his civil service examination test results because he had already used a veterans' preference at the time he was first hired by the Commonwealth. The Commission relied upon Management Directive 580.21, which set forth the rule allowing only one use of the veterans' preference. The court held that the Commission's decision finding that a veterans' preference may be used once, and once only, in the course of one's employment in the classified service of the Commonwealth was invalid. The court held that Management Directive 580.21(2)(d) was not consistent with the plain language of 51 Pa.C.S. § 7103(a), which mandated that a veteran received 10 additional points on every civil service examination whenever such an examination was successfully passed for a civil service appointment or promotional examination for a public position with the Commonwealth. As such, the court held that Management Directive 580.21(2)(d) was unenforceable to the extent it sought to limit the use of the preference to a one-time use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Commission's order and remanded the matter to the Commission with directions for it to add 10 points to the employee's rating on the PMA examination.


 

1850 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Allied Mech. & Elec., Inc. v. Pa. Prevailing Wage Appeals Bd.


No. 1743 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


923 A.2d 1220; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 233


April 9, 2007, Argued  
May 8, 2007, Decided  
May 8, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. PWAB-2A-2006. Prevailing Wage Appeals Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Secretary of the Pennsylvania Department of Labor and Industry ruled that petitioner contractor intentionally violated the Pennsylvania Prevailing Wage Act, 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 165-1 to 165-17, by failing to pay prevailing wages on certain public works projects and debarred it from contracting for any further projects for three years. Respondent Pennsylvania Prevailing Wage Appeals Board affirmed. The contractor sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Secretary found that the contractor used a set 6:2 ratio for prevailing wage projects (i.e., it paid skilled laborers such as electricians at laborers' rate for two hours of each day, regardless of the work performed), even after being advised that this was improper; and that it advised its employees to juggle their timecards to end up with this ratio. The appellate court held that this was substantial evidence in support of the Secretary's conclusion that the contractor intentionally violated § 5 (43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 165-5) of the Act. The Secretary was within its rights to rescind a hearing officer's decisional authority, and as the contractor had a full and fair opportunity to present its case, such rescission did not violate its rights to due process and a fair hearing. The Department's Bureau of Labor Law Compliance did not shift the burden of proof to the contractor. The contractor's "void for vagueness" claim failed; although neither the Act nor its regulations specifically defined laborers' tasks on any given prevailing wage project, the regulations appropriately relied on the custom and usage in the building and construction industry to give meaning to the term.


OUTCOME: The order of the Board was affirmed.


 

1851 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



R.L. Insulation Co., Inc. v. Prevailing Wage Appeals Bd.


No. 2018 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


923 A.2d 550; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 234


April 9, 2007, Argued  
May 8, 2007, Decided  
May 8, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. PWAB-4A-2005. State Agency: Prevailing Wage Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and its principals, challenged a decision of the Pennsylvania Prevailing Wage Appeals Board, affirming the adjudication and order of the Secretary of the Pennsylvania Department of Labor and Industry, who concluded that appellants had intentionally violated the Prevailing Wage Act (Act), 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 165-1 to 165-17, by failing to pay the prevailing wages due their workers on certain public works projects.


OVERVIEW: An investigation of the employer by the Pennsylvania Department of Labor and Industry's Bureau of Labor Law Compliance revealed that the employer had utilized set ratios for prevailing wage projects, regardless of the work being performed. Several workers testified that they were required to record certain of their hours at the lower laborer's rate, rather than the higher insulator's rate, even if they worked their entire shift as an insulator. The Secretary debarred and prohibited appellants from the award of any public works contract for a period of three years and awarded penalties and statutory damages. The court held that the testimony constituted substantial evidence in support of the Secretary's conclusion that appellants had intentionally violated the Act. The court also held that the Act was not unconstitutionally vague regarding the appropriate classification of laborers' work because appellants' violation of the Act was premised upon their utilization of set ratios for prevailing wage projects, regardless of the work being performed, not as the result of the Act's silence with respect to a specific definition of laborers' tasks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's decision.


 

1852 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Karnes v. AG


No. 609 M.D. 2005


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


921 A.2d 591; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 177


January 12, 2007, Submitted  
April 19, 2007, Decided  
April 19, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the state attorney general and the state police, filed preliminary objections seeking dismissal of the petition for review filed by petitioner inmate because it failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The inmate sought expungement of his DNA and fingerprint records retained pursuant to 2002 Pa. Laws 394 (Act 57) because the act was declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the constitutional violation that occurred in the enactment of Act 57 required the destruction of the inmate's DNA and fingerprint samples. The court found that the challenge to Act 57 was not to the substance of the law but to the procedure by which it was enacted. As such, the court did not invalidate Act 57 because the state's DNA testing of its prison population was categorically or per se unconstitutional nor did it hold that actions under Act 57 were nullified. Therefore, the inmate's DNA and fingerprint samples were not invalidated merely because Act 57 was held invalid. Because it was declared unconstitutional, Act 57 never had any effect on the law that it sought to repeal, namely, the DNA Detection of Sexual and Violent Offenders Act (DNA Act), 35 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 7651.101-7651.1102. The DNA Act was in effect when the inmate provided the DNA and fingerprint samples. The DNA Act authorized a statewide process for DNA identification of persons convicted of felony sex offenses and certain enumerated violent crimes, and it provided authority for the inmate's testing. Destruction of the inmate's DNA and fingerprint samples was not required.


OUTCOME: The preliminary objections filed by respondents were sustained, and the petition for review was dismissed.

 

1853 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Maurice A. Nernberg & Assocs. v. Coyne


No. 1593 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


920 A.2d 967; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 137


February 5, 2007, Argued  
April 4, 2007, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law firm challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, which denied its petition for money damages and counsel fees in connection with a successful mandamus action against the defendants, a prothonotary and a motions clerk, of the trial court. The firm claimed that 42 Pa.C.S. § 8303, entitled it to damages as a successful plaintiff in mandamus and 42 Pa.C.S. § 2503 entitled it to counsel fees.


OVERVIEW: The firm filed a complaint in mandamus with the trial court alleging that the prothonotary and clerk engaged in a discriminatory practice by permitting attorneys outside of the county to file preliminary objections through the mail, yet mandating that attorneys within the county personally file preliminary objections with the prothonotary and clerk. The prothonotary and clerk' refusal, according to the firm, forced it to send one of its employees to personally file documents, costing both time and money. The firm asserted that these damages were incident to the prothonotary and clerk' failure to accept filings by mail. Moreover, the firm argued that damages were recoverable even when not claimed in the pleadings. However, because the firm failed to request damages in its amended complaint in mandamus, pursuant to Pa.R.C.P. No. 1095, it was precluded from recovering damages. Also, there was no evidence to demonstrate that the prothonotary and clerk acted in bad faith. 42 Pa. C.S. § 2503(9) did not authorize an award of counsel fees to a pro se litigant. Because it represented itself in this litigation, the firm, acted pro se, precluding an award of counsel fees.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny mandamus damages.

Spahn v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by, Reconsideration denied by, En banc Spahn v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment, 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 780 (Pa. Commw. Ct., May 30, 2007)
Appeal granted by Spahn v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment, 598 Pa. 108, 954 A.2d 567, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1096 (2008)
Affirmed by Spahn v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment, 2009 Pa. LEXIS 1696 (Pa., Aug. 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. 0111 and 0115 September Term, 2005. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Judge Dych, J.
Spahn v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment, 874 A.2d 178, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 267 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer filed consolidated appeals of separate but identical orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) which granted the motion to quash filed on behalf of appellee property owner and dismissed the taxpayer's appeal for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The property owner owned two vacant lots in Philadelphia which were in an area zoned R-10 Residential District. The property owner filed two separate applications with the Department of Licenses and Inspections to construct a single family dwelling on each respective lot. The Department denied each application. The property owner appealed to the zoning board of adjustment and sought a dimensional variance as to each lot. The board concluded the property owner presented sufficient evidence for a variance. The taxpayer appealed. The trial court concluded that Philadelphia, Pa., Zoning Code § 14-1807(1) was subordinate to the General Assembly's enactment of § 17.1 of the First Class City Home Rule Act, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 13131.1. The appellate court held that as the taxpayer failed to present evidence establishing himself as an aggrieved party, he did not have standing to prosecute the appeals. Contrary to the taxpayer's argument, the bill at issue did not involve two, unrelated subjects. Thus, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 13131.1 was not violative of the single-subject rule under Pa. Const. art. III, § 3.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Nutter v. Dougherty


No. 2304 C.D. 2006, No. 2361 C.D. 2006, No. 2375 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


921 A.2d 44; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 132


March 7, 2007 Decided April 2, 2007, Argued  
April 2, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
 
Appeal granted by, Application denied by Nutter v. Dougherty, 591 Pa. 739, 921 A.2d 499, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 827 (2007)
Appeal granted by Nutter v. Dougherty, 922 A.2d 873, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 888 (Pa., 2007)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Nutter v. Dougherty, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2933 (Pa., Dec. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from No. 1516, April Term 2006. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Judge Tereshko, J.
Nutter v. Dougherty, 2007 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 101 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former city councilman, challenged the orders of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his complaint seeking declaratory relief against defendants, four politicians, and declared an ordinance on campaign financing void. Intervenor, the City of Philadelphia, also appealed, and one defendant cross-appealed the sustainment of plaintiff's preliminary objections to a counterclaim.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's suit sought a declaration from the trial court that defendants, who were possible mayoral candidates, were required to abide by campaign contribution dollar limits set forth in the city ordinance. Plaintiff asserted that defendants received illegal contributions in violation of the ordinance. The trial court granted defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings, concluding that the ordinance was unconstitutional, void, and unenforceable. The court determined that the trial court erred in granting defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings based on the Pennsylvania Constitution, the Home Rule Act, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 13131 and 13133, and the City's Home Rule Charter, which granted the City complete powers of legislation and administration with regard to its municipal functions, except as to when the legislature had expressly or impliedly indicated its intent to assume exclusive jurisdiction over a field. Because the Pennsylvania legislature had indicated no intent to assume exclusive jurisdiction over the field of campaign finance in connection with setting contribution limits for local elective office, the ordinance was constitutional and enforceable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court granting defendants' motions for judgment on the pleadings and that declared the ordinance unconstitutional. The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the counterclaim of one defendant as moot.


 

1856 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Daugherty v. County of Allegheny


No. 1777 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


920 A.2d 936; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 127


February 5, 2007, Argued  
March 27, 2007, Decided  
March 27, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. GD06-013464. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Wettick, Jr., A.J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county and its board of property assessment review appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which struck down a rule adopted by the board with respect to assessment appeals. The board's rule limited the scope of appellee taxpayers' appeal to the question of whether the base year market value assigned to the taxpayers' property in the last county-wide assessment was correct.


OVERVIEW: The rule at issue prohibited taxpayers from challenging their assessment for the simple reason that it exceeded the property's current market value. The court agreed that the board lacked the statutory authority to limit assessment appeals in that way. 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5452.10 gave the taxpayer the ability to challenge its assessment for the reason that the base year market value no longer reflected the property's current market value. It was the taxpayer's decision which theory to pursue in its assessment appeal, i.e., that the assessment exceeded the current market value or the assessment was based upon an incorrect base year market value. Once that valuation was determined in accordance with the appeal it was to stand as the valuation for the assessment of all county taxes. The trial court did not err in declaring the rule's limitation on assessment appeals to be invalid, as the rule impermissibly circumscribed the taxpayers' appeal rights that were guaranteed in 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5452.10.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


 

1857 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re Nomination Petitions of Owen


No. 124 M.D. 2007


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


922 A.2d 973; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 199


March 21, 2007, Heard  
March 23, 2007, Decided  
March 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Publication Ordered May 2, 2007.
Affirmed by In re Nomination Petitions of Owen, 592 Pa. 17, 922 A.2d 878, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 951 (Pa., Apr. 30, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, members of the Republican and Democratic parties, filed objections to the nomination petition of respondent judicial candidate based on the candidate's failure to file a statement of financial interests with the Pennsylvania Ethics Commission as required by the Ethics Act, 65 Pa.C.S. § 1104(b).


OVERVIEW: The candidate, who already held another judicial office, attached a statement of financial interests to his nomination petitions but did not make a separate filing with the Commission. He testified that he had received both written and oral advice from Commission that as an incumbent judicial officer, he was not required to file the statement with the Commission. The advice was apparently based on the Kremer decision, which concluded that sitting jurists were not subject to the Ethics Act because application of the Act would infringe on the supreme court's general supervisory and administrative authority over the courts. The court found that in relying on both the written and oral advice of the Commission, the candidate had "substantially complied" with § 1104(b). The court also ruled that requiring all candidates to file the financial statements with the Commission and to append copies thereof to their nominating petitions did not violate the separation of powers and was not prohibited by Kremer. Because the candidate substantially complied, and because the constitutional issue involved was one of first impression, the court applied its decision prospectively.


OUTCOME: The objections were denied and the Secretary of the Commonwealth was directed to include the candidate's name on the ballot in the May 2007 Primary Election.

Ethan-Michael, Inc. v. Bd. of Supervisors


No. 1048 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


918 A.2d 203; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 105


November 13, 2006, Argued  
March 8, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. 06-1685. Common Pleas Court of the County of Berks, Judge Lieberman, J.
Ethan-Michael, Inc. v. Bd. of Supervisors of Union Twp., 2006 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 561 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania) which affirmed the decision of an appointed Hearing Officer in favor of appellee Board of Supervisors and determined that certain provisions of Union Township, Pa., Zoning Ordinance § 905.3 were unconstitutional and invalidated and severed them but otherwise upheld the Ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The property owner owned property in an AP-Agricultural Preservation District. The Hearing Officer rejected claims of exclusion. The Hearing Officer concluded that the legislative judgment did not violate substantive due process and that Union Township, Pa., Zoning Ordinance § 401.1 passed muster, based on balancing the rights of the property owner to be free of undue restrictions on its use of property against the public policy of the state, county and Township to encourage active farming on large contiguous tracts. The Hearing Officer decided that any inconsistency was not fatal. The Hearing Officer granted the validity challenge to the extent of invalidating Union Township, Pa., Zoning Ordinance, § 905.3(E), (F) and (I) and severing them, but he denied all remaining requests. The appellate court agreed that the property owner's assertions regarding intent were unavailing. The stated purpose of the Ordinance was to preserve prime agricultural soils, and the Ordinance accomplished that purpose. The Ordinance was a valid exercise of police power as it is substantially related to the purpose that it purported to serve.


OUTCOME: The Hearing Officer committed no error in his decision to invalidate and to sever the Ordinance but otherwise to sustain the Ordinance and to deny the curative amendment requested by the property owner. The trial court's order was affirmed.

Weaver v. Franklin County


No. 1463 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


918 A.2d 194; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 104


December 22, 2006, Submitted  
March 7, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Weaver v. Franklin County, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1594 (Pa., Aug. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. A.D. 2006-1059. Common Pleas Court of the County of Franklin. Judge Rehkamp, President Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendant county, alleging its unnamed employees were guilty of negligence, intentional infliction of emotional distress (IIED), civil conspiracy, and libel in connection with his prosecution and imprisonment for sexual assault. The Franklin County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) sustained the county's preliminary objections on the ground it was immune from suit under 42 Pa.C.S. § 8541. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged county employees interfered with his rights in his trial, appeals, post-conviction relief petitions, and civil suits, resulting in his illegal incarceration. As he could not identify the responsible employees, he invoked respondeat superior. The appellate court held that his civil conspiracy, IIED, and libel claims failed because the county was not liable under 42 Pa.C.S. § 8550 for its employees' intentional torts. His claim that the county negligently failed to transmit records and docket pleadings failed as these acts did not fall within 42 Pa.C.S. § 8542(b)'s exceptions to immunity. While his allegations could have supported a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action asserting a violation of his right of access to the courts, the claim failed because he could not identify the employees who allegedly committed the wrongful acts. Whether viewed as a state tort claim or as a federal civil rights claim, his civil conspiracy claim failed; as he could not recover for the underlying torts of IIED and libel, there could be no conspiracy as to them. His request to amend his complaint under Pa.R.C.P. No. 1033 was properly denied, as an amendment would not have cured its defects.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Brown v. Montgomery County


No. 704 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


918 A.2d 802; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 70


November 22, 2006, Submitted  
February 21, 2007, Decided  
February 21, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. 05-24712. Common Pleas Court of the County of Montgomery. Smyth, J.
Brown v. Montgomery County, 2006 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 219 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of an order from the Common Pleas Court of the County of Montgomery (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his complaint against appellees, a county and various county taxing authorities and officials, with prejudice. The owner had filed an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, seeking relief based on the alleged improper assessment of real estate taxes. Appellees' motion for sanctions was denied.


OVERVIEW: The owner entered into a trust agreement, wherein the property he resided on became the sole corpus thereof. There was no particular purpose declared for the trust. Believing that the property was free from taxation under the Contract Clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, the owner filed his action in both his individual and joint trustee capacity. A prior identical action was dismissed for failure to have followed the statutory procedures of the General County Assessment Law, 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 5020-1 - 5020-602. A similar action in federal court was also dismissed. Thereafter, the owner's request for real estate tax exemption was denied by the county board of assessment appeals. Rather than seeking judicial review, the owner filed the instant action, which was dismissed with prejudice. The trial court denied appellees' sanction motion. On appeal, the court found that the state statutory procedures provided the owner with an adequate remedy, and he could assert his claims of statutory unconstitutionality on judicial review of any determination made. As he had relentlessly pursued a meritless claim using the wrong procedure, sanctions were deemed appropriate under Pa.R.A.P. 2744.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court and imposed a sanction of reasonable attorney fees to appellees. The matter was remanded to the trial court to determine the appropriate amount of fees to be awarded.


 

1861 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



WRC N. Fork Heights, Inc. v. Bd. of Assessment Appeals


No. 1939 C.D. 2005


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


917 A.2d 893; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 65


October 18, 2006, Argued  
February 20, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by WRC N. Fork Heights, Inc. v. Bd. of Assessment Appeals, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1491 (Pa., July 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Common Pleas Court of the County of Jefferson. Appealed from No. 841 - 2004 CD State Agency. Judge Foradora, President Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought a real estate tax exemption under § 204(a)(3) (72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5020-204(a)(3)) of the Pennsylvania General County Assessment Law. Appellee board of assessment appeals denied the request. The taxpayer appealed; the Jefferson County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) affirmed. The taxpayer sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer provided low-income housing for the elderly and received subsidies under the federal Section 202 Program. It claimed it met the requirements of § 204(a)(3) of the Assessment Law and was thus automatically deemed to be a "purely public charity" that did not have to satisfy the Hospital Utilization Project's (HUP's) five-prong test for exemption under the Pennsylvania Institutions of Purely Public Charity Act, 10 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 371- 385. The appellate court disagreed; an entity seeking a statutory tax exemption had to establish it was a "purely public charity" under Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 2 before a court could reach the question of whether it was entitled to a statutory exemption. The taxpayer waived its claims as to its compliance with the Charity Act because it did not present them to the trial court. It did not meet the second prong of the HUP test as it did not show it donated a "substantial portion" of its services; its residents paid rent that was then subsidized by the U.S. government. As to the fourth prong, it did not show it was abating government costs, as its rents were not below the market rate; it was merely a Section 202 Program housing provider.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order of the trial court.

City of Philadelphia v. FOP Lodge No. 5


No. 1040 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


916 A.2d 1210; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 25; 182 L.R.R.M. 2826


November 14, 2006, Argued  
January 26, 2007, Decided  
January 26, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by City of Philadelphia v. FOP Lodge No. 5, 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 125 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Mar. 16, 2007)
Appeal denied by City of Phila. v. FOP Lodge No. 5, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1727 (Pa., Aug. 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: City of Philadelphia [**1] Appealed from No. 0961, February Term 2006. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Judge Dych, J.
City of Philadelphia v. FOP, Lodge No. 5, 2006 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 271 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the Pennsylvania Policemen and Firemen Collective Bargaining Act (Act 111), appellant city and appellee police union convened an arbitration panel to decide terms of employment. The city petitioned to vacate the award, claiming the panel violated the Pennsylvania Intergovernmental Cooperation Authority Act for Cities of the First Class (PICA). The Philadelphia County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) denied relief; the city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The arbitration award increased the city's contribution for current and retired police officers' health care coverage. The city claimed the panel violated PICA by failing to accord substantial weight to the city's five-year financial plan and its ability to pay the increased award without adversely affecting city services, and by finding the city had the ability to pay the increased award. Applying an extreme standard of deference to Act 111 arbitration awards, the trial court declined to review the arbitrators' findings of law and fact and denied the city's petition. The union contended that courts could not review Act 111 awards for legal or factual error. The appellate court disagreed. The clear language of § 209(k) (53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 12720.209(k)) of PICA required the trial court to review an arbitration award entered pursuant to Act 11 to determine whether the arbitrators accorded substantial weight to the city's five-year financial plan and its ability to pay increased award without adversely affecting city services. Because the trial court applied a narrow certiorari scope of review, it did not reach the merits of the award.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the order of the trial court and remanded for consideration on the merits so that the trial court could apply the proper standard of review articulated under PICA in accordance with the appellate court's opinion.

Lamar Adver. of Penn., LLC v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 1403 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


915 A.2d 705; 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 15


December 12, 2006, Argued  
January 18, 2007, Decided  
January 18, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Lamar Adver. of Penn, LLC v. Zoning Hearing Bd., 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1419 (Pa., July 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. S-1223-2005. Common Pleas Court of the County of Schuylkill. Stine, J.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an advertising company, challenged an order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Schuylkill (Pennsylvania) that denied the company's appeal of a decision of a zoning board denying the company's application for a variance from height and area requirements for an off-site advertising sign.


OVERVIEW: The board determined that the company failed to meet the threshold requirements to establish entitlement to a variance to allow the company to build an advertising sign that was higher and larger than allowed by the borough's zoning ordinance. The appellate court held that the fact that the board determined that the ordinance included a de jure exclusion concerning off-site billboards did not automatically permit the company to erect whatever kind of structure it wished without investigation into the reasonableness of the proposed plans. The appellate court held that the board's explanation as to why it utilized the existing provisions of the zoning ordinance in order to rectify the unconstitutional infirmity was supported by substantial evidence of record. Therefore, the Board's use of the same regulations for on-site and off-site advertising signs was appropriate under the circumstances. Furthermore, the appellate court held that because the record contained proof reflecting the existence of advertising signs that met the size restrictions set forth in the zoning ordinance, there was no de facto exclusion.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Doherty v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 901 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


921 A.2d 532; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 745


November 16, 2006, Argued  
December 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Reported at DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing v. Doherty, 912 A.2d 930, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 730 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from No. 05-10388. Common Pleas Court of the County of Chester, Hall, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation (DOT), sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the statutory appeal of appellee licensee from the requirement that he comply with 2000 Pa. Laws 63 (Act 63), formerly 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 7001-7003 (repealed), relating to ignition interlock devices. The current interlock requirements were found at 75 Pa.C.S. § 3801.


OVERVIEW: The licensee had been convicted on a driving under the influence (DUI) charge on November 21, 2000; the licensee had two prior DUI convictions from 1997. Pursuant to former 42 Pa.C.S. § 7002(2), as a condition precedent to the restoration of the licensee's operating privilege, he was required to install an ignition interlock system on his vehicles. The DOT provided the notice authorized by 75 Pa.C.S. § 1542(d) that the licensee's operating privilege was revoked for five years as a habitual offender. The licensee was granted nunc pro nunc relief as to the interlock requirement due to the trial court's interpretation that the triggering DUI offense, which occurred on November 30, 1999, took place prior to September 30, 2000, the effective date of Act 63. However, the court reversed because the language of 2000 Pa. Laws 63, § 3 clearly stated that the interlock requirement applied to all persons convicted of a second or subsequent violation of 75 Pa.C.S. § 3731 on or after the Act's effective date. Because the licensee was convicted of his third DUI on November 21, 2000, the interlock requirement was properly applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

 

1865 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Rothstein v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 856 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


922 A.2d 17; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 746


November 3, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
December 18, 2006, Decided  
December 18, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Publication Ordered April 16, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. CI-05-11348. Common Pleas Court of the County of Lancaster. Ashworth, J.
DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing v. Rothstein, 912 A.2d 929, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 716 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, Bureau of Motor Vehicles (DOT), sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which granted the appeal of appellee licensee and ordered that DOT's cancellation of the licensee's operator's license be rescinded. The trial court concluded in its order that an earlier version of 75 Pa.C.S. § 1572 applied.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was convicted in New Jersey of operating a motor vehicle while in possession of a controlled substance. His ability to obtain a New Jersey Driver's license was suspended. The DOT learned of the suspension and issued a notice of cancellation of the licensee's driver's license. The trial court ordered that the cancellation be rescinded. The appellate court held that the court was to look to the licensee's current operating privilege status and the current 75 Pa.C.S. § 1572 of the Motor Vehicle Code in determining whether the licensee's license was properly cancelled by DOT based on an old conviction. A suspension based on that old conviction continued due to the licenssee's failure to pay a license restoration fee. Hence, the trial court erred in applying the older version of 75 Pa.C.S. § 1572. Further, the cancellation was proper under § 1572(a)(1)(i) because the licensee was not entitled to have his license renewed under 75 Pa.C.S. § 1503(a)(1) as a result of the current suspension of his operating privileges in New Jersey. Given the prompt issuance of the notice of cancellation, there was no due process violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

Salters v. Pa. State Police Mun. Police Officers' Educ. & Training Comm'n


No. 761 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


912 A.2d 347; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 632


October 17, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
November 29, 2006, Decided  
November 29, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. 33280. Municipal Police Officers' Education & Training Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Pennsylvania State Police Municipal Police Officers' Education and Training Commission revoked petitioner applicant's certification as a municipal police officer on grounds he made a false statement on his certification application in violation of 34 Pa. Code § 203.14(a)(7). The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After evaluating the applicant, a psychologist found he was a psychological risk to be a police officer. He obtained a second evaluation from another psychologist, who found no impediment to his serving as an officer. The application asked if he had undergone any other psychological evaluation in the past year; he answered "no." After a hearing, the Commission revoked his certification under 37 Pa. Code § 203.14(a)(5) for filing a fraudulent application in violation of 34 Pa. Code § 203.14(a)(7), and under 34 Pa. Code § 203.14(a)(7) and (a)(8), because it had issued his certification in error. He claimed his due process rights were violated because the Commission amended its revocation notice to add two other charges after he exercised his right to a hearing. The court held that as the amendment was filed 30 days before the hearing, his due process rights were not violated because he had ample time to prepare his defense. The record supported the Commission's findings. That he allegedly submitted the false application due to pressure from his boss was not a defense. No precedent supported his theory that only agency heads who were attorneys could adjudicate administrative hearings.


OUTCOME: The Commission's ruling was affirmed.

Christ the King Manor v. Dep't of Pub. Welfare


No. 251 M.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


911 A.2d 624; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 623


September 13, 2006 Decided November 22, 2006, Argued  
November 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed without opinion by Christ the King Manor v. Dep't of Pub. Welfare, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1205 (Pa., July 23, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Department of Public Welfare (DPW), filed preliminary objections with regard to the amended petition for review filed by petitioners, 24 nursing facilities participating in the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania's medical assistance (Medicaid) program. Petitioners challenged the validity of regulation amendments to nursing facility payment rates and sought a declaration that the amended regulations were unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners asserted that the amendments to the regulations were authorized by 2005 Pa. Laws 177, which was allegedly unconstitutional on several grounds. Petitioners' amended petition for review sought to increase funding by invalidating the cost adjustment regulation amendments. Petitioners requested a declaration that the cost adjustment regulations were invalid and sought a permanent injunction requiring DPW to set rates for fiscal year 2005-06 using the pre-amendment regulations. The court found no constitutional infirmity with regard to the enacted regulation amendments, finding that the amendments maintained a single unifying subject and that neither the Pennsylvania legislators nor the public were actually deceived by the contents of the house bill regarding the amendments. As such, the court found that petitioners failed to plead a violation of the clear title rule set forth in Pa. Const. art. III, § 3. The court also determined that the original purpose of the house bill did not change by enactment of the amendments. The court also upheld the delegation of regulation changes to DPW as within the scope of the federal Medicaid Act and the Pennsylvania Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court sustained DPW's preliminary objections and dismissed petitioners' amended petition. The court sustained DPW's demurrers to all eight counts of petitioners' amended petition for review as well as dismissed petitioners' motion for class certification as moot.

City of Pittsburgh v. FOP, Fort Pitt Lodge No. 1


No. 56 C.D. 2004, No. 57 C.D. 2004


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


911 A.2d 651; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 624


October 16, 2006, Argued  
November 22, 2006, Decided  
November 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by City of Pittsburgh v. FOP, 926 A.2d 437, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1090 (Pa., 2007)
Affirmed by City of Pittsburgh v. Fop, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2452 (Pa., Nov. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. S.A. 03-202 and S.A. 03-205. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Judge Watson, Senior Judge.
City of Pittsburgh v. FOP, Fort Pitt Lodge No. 1, 584 Pa. 575, 886 A.2d 682, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2674 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police union sued appellee city seeking to vacate an arbitration panel's award that capped the city's contributions toward future retiree medical benefits. A trial court upheld the award, and the commonwealth court affirmed. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court remanded for determination of whether the reduction of post-retirement health care benefits for active officers conflicted with a prior supreme court decision.


OVERVIEW: When the city and the union were unable to reach agreement on terms of a successor collective bargaining agreement relating to medical benefits, the union demanded interest arbitration. The arbitration award capped the city's contribution toward the cost of future police retirees' medical insurance at an amount equal to that paid by the city for such coverage on the date of an officer's retirement. The commonwealth court's decision that consensual modification of future retirees' benefits was constitutionally permissible was remanded for consideration of whether 53 Pa.C.S. § 2962(c)(3), as interpreted by the supreme court, precluded the arbitration panel from reducing post-retirement medical benefits for officers who had not yet retired. The commonwealth court found no conflict between its prior decision and either § 2962(c)(3) or the supreme court's decision in Appeal of Upper Providence Township. The supreme court's decision concerned the statute's prohibition against diminishment of rights of former employees, and § 2962(c)(3) did not apply to changes to present employees' benefits that arose under contract rather than under a statutory pension or retirement system.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment upholding the arbitrator's award was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Auto Mart, Inc.


No. 2055 C.D. 2005


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


910 A.2d 171; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 610


October 17, 2006, Argued  
November 15, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. G.D. 87-19169. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Farino, Senior Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the owner of an auto sales mart, challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which discharged his previously entered rule to show cause. As a result of a criminal investigation regarding inaccurate odometer readings and the sale of defective motor vehicles, the Commonwealth, acting through the Attorney General (AG), entered into an assurance of voluntary compliance (AVC) with the owner.


OVERVIEW: Under the AVC, the owner agreed to pay civil penalties; forfeit the right to do business in any capacity in the automotive industry in the Commonwealth; recognize the trial court's jurisdiction over the AVC; and comply with relevant statutes. The owner had petitioned for a rule to show cause why the AVC should not be modified to allow him to maintain his license, essentially to modify his signed AVC agreement, which had been filed in 1987. On appeal, the owner asserted that the rule to show cause was final and appealable because it carried the effect of putting the losing party out of court. The court agreed that the trial court's dissolution of the rule to show cause was final and appealable since the trial court's decision terminated the owner's action to modify the AVC and forced him to either appeal or file another action. However, the court upheld the discharge because the rule to show case was not the proper vehicle to amend the AVC. Upon filing the signed AVC, the matter between the owner and the AG was closed and had to be reopened by the AG under 73 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 201-5 for any change to be addressed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Pa. Bankers Ass'n v. Pa. Dep't of Banking


No. 397 M.D. 2005


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


910 A.2d 767; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 605


September 11, 2006, Submitted  
November 13, 2006, Decided  
November 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part, Stay granted by Pa. Bankers Ass'n v. Pa. Dep't of Banking, 592 Pa. 14, 922 A.2d 876, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 925 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Pa. Bankers Ass'n v. Pa. Dep't of Banking, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 2261 (Pa., Dec. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to 10 Pa. Code § 3.6, petitioner banks protested respondent credit union's charter conversion application. Respondent Pennsylvania Department of Banking denied the banks' request for a hearing on their protest, and deemed the credit union's application approved under 17 Pa.C.S. § 501(g). The banks appealed.


OVERVIEW: The credit union filed a notice with the Department that it intended to convert its charter from an occupation-based credit union to a community credit union. The banks filed a protest under 10 Pa. Code § 3.5(a) and requested a hearing and leave to inspect and copy the hearing file. The Department denied these requests. The credit union informed the Department that, as it failed to act within 30 days of receipt of the charter conversion notice, the notice was deemed approved under 17 Pa.C.S. § 501(g); the Department agreed. The court held that the Department's failure to act by conducting a hearing prior to the deemed approval violated 10 Pa. Code § 3.6's mandatory hearing rule, which applied to the credit union's application. Because the requirements of procedural due process in an application protest proceeding included access to the application and supporting data, the banks were entitled to have access to the hearing file under 10 Pa. Code § 3.4. Section 302 (71 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 733-302) of the Pennsylvania Department of Banking Code was unconstitutional to the extent that it prohibited application protesters from inspecting hearing files pursuant to 10 Pa. Code § 3.4.


OUTCOME: The Department's deemed approval of the credit union's charter conversion application was vacated and the case was remanded to the Department for a hearing conducted pursuant to 10 Pa. Code ch. 3.

Stilp v. Commonwealth


No. 1 M.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


910 A.2d 775; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 604


June 7, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
November 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application granted by, Judgment entered by Stilp v. Commonwealth, 929 A.2d 660, 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 379 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2007)
Affirmed by Stilp v. Pa., 2009 Pa. LEXIS 1319 (Pa., July 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Stilp v. Commonwealth, 699 A.2d 1353, 1997 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 372 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the Pennsylvania General Assembly, named legislative leaders of both parties, the Governor, and the Treasurer, filed preliminary objections to the original jurisdictional matter brought by petitioner, a resident taxpayer, challenging on constitutional grounds the availability to state legislators of anything of benefit beyond salary and mileage. Petitioner also challenged local grant monies and leadership accounts.


OVERVIEW: The basic premise of this lawsuit was that state legislators had access to things that benefitted them beyond that which was expressly permitted by the Pennsylvania Constitution. Petitioner sought various forms of relief, praying for declarations that the challenged benefits were unconstitutional and for injunctions restraining the Treasurer from disbursing future monies for the challenged purposes. Petitioner also sought mandatory injunctions compelling the return of unspent monies in leadership accounts and requiring legislative leaders to cooperate with an audit by the Auditor General. As to the demurrers, the court noted that the Pennsylvania Supreme Court had repeatedly rejected the position advanced by petitioner as to the claims based on Pa. Const. art. II, § 8. The court noted that petitioner did not allege that any change to salary and mileage was made that was received during the current term; therefore, no violation of art. II, § 8 was stated. The court found that petitioner failed to make allegations against the Governor as well as failed to make sufficient allegations against the Treasurer. Standing on the part of petitioner had already been resolved in his favor.


OUTCOME: The court sustained, in part, the preliminary objections with regard to the claims against the Governor, those against the Treasurer, the claims for audit relief, and cost of living expenses. The court overruled the preliminary objections as to standing, failure to join, no case or controversy, injuries, and surplus. The court also sustained the demurrers except to the surplus claim and granted petitioner leave to file a second amended petition.

Adams Outdoor Adver., L.P. v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 216 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


909 A.2d 469; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 547


September 14, 2006, Argued  
October 18, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Adams Outdoor Adver., L.P. v. Zoning Hearing Bd. of Smithfield Twp., 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1055 (Pa., May 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. 9000 Civil 2004. Common Pleas Court of the County of Monroe. Judge Vican, President Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant challenged the order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Monroe (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a decision of appellee, a township zoning hearing board that required the applicant to remove to off-premises advertising billboards it leased.


OVERVIEW: The applicant leased two billboards on a landowner's property. The landowner applied for a zoning permit to perform site alteration work. The township's zoning officer issued the permit subject to the condition that the two off-premises advertising billboards leased by the applicant be removed within 30 days, as required by an ordinance. On appeal, the applicant asserted that application of the ordinance resulted in a taking of its property without just compensation, infringed on its right to free speech, and selectively discriminated against properties on which off-premises advertising signs were located. The court held that requiring removal of the billboards was not an unlawful taking since the discontinuance was triggered by choice and action of the landowner, not by any municipal action. The court found that the applicant presented no evidence or argument to support its assertion that the ordinance violated its right to equal protection by treating off-premises signage differently from other uses, and the ordinance did not attempt to regulate signage based on content or effectuate a total ban on commercial speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Rebert v. York County Detectives Ass'n


No. 659 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


909 A.2d 906; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 544


September 12, 2006, Argued  
October 16, 2006, Decided  
October 16, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from No. 2005-SU-002070-Y08. Common Pleas Court of the County of York. Judge Blackwell, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the District Attorney for York County, challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of York County (New York), which affirmed the Act 111 grievance arbitration award directing the District Attorney's office to refrain from scheduling work hours inconsistent with Article V of its Collective Bargaining Agreement (CBA) with appellee, the York County Detectives Association (the union).


OVERVIEW: The CBA established that the workweek was to consist of five consecutive work days in a pre-established work schedule for a total of 40 hours per week. The regular work day consisted of 8.5 scheduled consecutive hours, which included an unpaid one-half hour lunch. After the District Attorney hired a detective to work a schedule deviating from those provisions, the union filed a grievance seeking compliance with the CBA. The arbitrator agreed with the union and sustained the grievance, concluding that 16 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 1620 was not relevant to the matter and that the establishing the work hours was a matter separate from hiring, firing, or supervising employees since the parties negotiated the limitation on work hours. The District Attorney contended that, in light of the reservation of exclusive authority to hire, fire, and supervise its employees conferred by § 1620, the arbitrator lacked jurisdiction, exceeded his powers, and impaired constitutional rights when he enforced the CBA. The court disagreed and upheld the arbitrator's decision, finding that work hours constituted a term or condition of employment and were a mandatory subject of bargaining under Act 111.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

McElheney v. Workers' Comp. Appeal Bd. (Kvaerner Philadelphia Shipyard)


No. 806 C.D. 2006


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


908 A.2d 960; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 509


August 18, 2006, Submitted  
September 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by McElheney v. Workers' Comp. Appeal Bd. (Kvaerner Phila. Shipyard), 592 Pa. 769, 923 A.2d 1175, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1094 (2007)
Affirmed by Daniel McElheney v. Workers' Comp. Appeal Bd., 2008 Pa. LEXIS 97 (Pa., Feb. 19, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Appeal Board ruled that petitioner claimant was not entitled to benefits under the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Act, 77 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 1-1041.4; 2501-2626, because his sole remedy was under the Longshore and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act (LHWCA), 33 U.S.C.S. §§ 901-950. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was working on a ship in a graven dry dock -- i.e., a dry dock dug into the land -- at the time he was injured. A workers' compensation judge (WCJ) found that the claimant's exclusive remedy was under the LHWCA because working on a ship in dry dock was a traditional maritime activity precluding access to Pennsylvania workers' compensation benefits. The claimant appealed, and the Board affirmed. The court, analyzing the legislative history of the LHWCA and the case law construing it, held that because the claimant was injured in a graven dry dock while the ship was not afloat, he was on land "in a physical sense" at the time of the injury and thus had access to both to both LHWCA and Pennsylvania workers' compensation benefits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the WCJ and the Board's finding that the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Act did not apply and remanded for a determination as to whether the claimant was entitled to benefits.

Soc'y Created to Reduce Urban Blight v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


No. 2099 C.D. 2005, No. 2192 C.D. 2005

908 A.2d 967; 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 510
