Prince v. Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review


No. 658 C.D. 2003


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


832 A.2d 583; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 684; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P12,435


July 25, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
September 23, 2003, Decided  
September 23, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. B-408679. State Agency, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed from an adjudication of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which denied her claim for unemployment benefits, affirming the referee's determination that she was ineligible for benefits due to her employment by her son pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 753(l)(4)(5).


OVERVIEW: The claimant worked part-time for a law firm that was wholly owned by her son until such time as she was terminated. At that time, she sought unemployment benefits, which were denied to her based on her ineligibility under § 753(l)(4)(5). The Board affirmed the decision of the referee, and the claimant sought judicial review. The claimant sought to overturn prior case law that held that the classification contained in § 753(l)(4)(5) was constitutional. The court initially noted that because family relationships were not suspect classifications, the rational relationship test of U.S. Const. amend. XIV was applicable to the claimant's equal protection challenge. However, the court found that such case law was valid, in that the classification was rationally related to an important state interest of avoiding potential fraud among family members. The court found that the claimant had not met her burden of proving that the classification scheme was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the adjudication of the Board.

 

1984 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re Nomination Paper of Zulick


No. 534 M.D. 2003


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


832 A.2d 572; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 682


September 9, 2003, Argued  
September 19, 2003, Decided  
September 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended September 26, 2003.
Affirmed by, Without opinion by In re Nomination of Zulick, 834 A.2d 1126, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1967 (Pa., Oct. 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.



DISPOSITION: Petition to set aside nomination paper granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner objector filed a petition to set aside the nomination petition of respondent candidate, who was listed as a minor party candidate in a municipal election for the office of common pleas court judge, based on his having unsuccessfully run as a candidate in the primary elections of the major political parties previously, in violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, §§ 2911(e)(5), 2936.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was cross-filed on the Republican and Democratic ballots for a judgeship position, but was defeated on both tickets in those parties' primary elections. Thereafter, the Reform party asked him to become their candidate. He obtained the requisite signatures and completed a candidate's affidavit. The objector filed her petition to set aside the candidate's nomination petition, alleging that because he ran on the other two ballots in the May, 2003 primary, he was forbidden from being the minor party's candidate in the November, 2003 general election. The court initially reviewed case law from other ballot access cases and determined that an intermediate level of scrutiny was applicable under the equal protection challenge of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court found that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, §§ 2911(e)(5), 2936 were constitutional, in that the importance of the state's interest in foreclosing the nomination of "sore losers" justified the burden imposed on minor political parties. There was no invidious discrimination found by the restrictions, which the court held did not unfairly or unnecessarily burden the "availability of political opportunity."


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition.

 

1985 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Bronson v. Horn


No. 1025 M.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


830 A.2d 1092; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 617


July 18, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
August 26, 2003, Decided  
August 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected September 17, 2003.
Affirmed by, Without opinion by Bronson v. Horn, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 488 (Pa., Mar. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's motion for summary judgment granted. Petition for review dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Commissioner of the Pennsylvania Department of Corrections moved for summary judgment in petitioner inmate's suit for a declaratory judgment that the Department's legal fees policy was unlawfully deprived him of access to the courts. The inmate also challenged the withholding his "idle pay."


OVERVIEW: The Department's policy limited to $ 10 a month the amount that the Department would place in an inmate account for legal mailings. The issue was whether the policy violated the inmate's access to the courts under federal law. The Department's stated reason for the policy was that it allowed it to continue to provide inmates with access to the courts, while taking into consideration: (1) the need for consistent application of the policy and practices throughout the state's correctional institutions; and (2) the Department's fiscal responsibility to the taxpayers. The court found that the evidence established a rational connection between the regulation and a legitimate neutral governmental interest. It permitted court access, limited the funds advanced equally for each indigent inmate, and held a line on taxpayer monies employed for that purpose. Moreover, the Department persuasively argued that because the money was coming from its own budget, it had to curtail the amounts available for other important programs. The policy passed constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted and the petition was dismissed.

 

1986 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lyons


No. 3062 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


830 A.2d 663; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 609


June 27, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
August 20, 2003, Decided  
August 20, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From Nos. 85-10,547; 85-11,110; 85-11,235; 86-10,164 86-10,440; 86-10,461; 87-10,411; 92-11,646; 95-10,213; 95-10,788. Common Pleas Court of the County of Lycoming. Judge ANDERSON.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania) denied a request by petitioner, a prisoner, to "quash" costs, fines, and restitution. The prisoner appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court cost clerk sent a financial obligation form to the Department of Corrections seeking payment from the prisoner's inmate account pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9728(b)(5), commonly referred to as Act 84. The money was to be used to pay costs, fines, and restitution ordered as part of the prisoner's sentences, all of which were at least several years old. The prisoner sought to have the costs, fines, and restitution quashed because he fully served the confinement and supervision portions of his remote sentences before the Act 84 deductions were taken. The appellate court held that what the prisoner actually sought was a modification of his sentences to remove payment of costs, fines, and restitution. The prisoner filed his papers in the instant matter seven years after the last sentence at issue was entered. Seven years was well past the allowed periods for seeking modification of costs and fines. The prisoner also argued that he was entitled to reimbursement of money deducted from his inmate account prior to the trial court's order to stop the deductions. The appellate court found that Act 84 clearly authorized the deductions taken, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9728(b)(5).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1987 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Hosp. & Healthsystem Assn of Pa. v. Dep't of Pub. Welfare


No. 840 M.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


828 A.2d 1196; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 524


March 5, 2003, Argued  
July 23, 2003, Decided  
July 23, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Hosp. & Healthsystem Ass'n of Pa. v. Dep't of Pub. Welfare, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2975 (Pa., Dec. 27, 2005)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Respondent Department of Public Welfare's petition for review dismissed. Respondents' preliminary objections sustained in part and overruled in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a hospital trade association and three non-profit hospitals, sought to enjoin certain provisions of the General Appropriations Act of 2002 (the 2002 GAA) S.5, 186th Gen. Assem., Reg. Sess. (Pa. 2002), which it claimed improperly changed the substantive law on reimbursement to providers who treated Medical Assistance (MA) recipients. Respondents, the Department of Public Welfare (DPW) and its Secretary, moved to dismiss the petition.


OVERVIEW: Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 40, § 991.2116 (Act 68), guaranteed a managed care organization (MCO) "reasonably necessary costs." Petitioners argued that the 2002 GAA, which capped the DPW's fee-for-service rate when a provider was not under contract with the MCO in which a MA recipient was enrolled, conflicted with Act 68 and violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 11. The court rejected petitioners' claims. Petitioners had standing to maintain their action because they sought to protect a substantial interest, namely, the right of a hospital to negotiate with a MCO for payment of emergency services provided to MA recipients. The court agreed with respondents, however, that the disputed provision in the 2002 GAA was not a rate-setting statute and thus did not effect a change in the substantive law. A general appropriations bill could include limitations on the expenditure of funds, and the disputed provision limited the amount of public funds that could be used to reimburse noncontracting service providers. The provision did not conflict with Act 68, pursuant to which DPW had to pay for the "reasonably necessary costs" of inpatient care; those costs were specified in DPW's fee-for-service schedule.


OUTCOME: The court sustained DPW's preliminary objections, except its challenge to petitioners' standing, and the court dismissed petitioners' request for review.

 

1988 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Rising Sun Entm't, Inc. v. Bureau of Liquor Control Enforcement


No. 3073 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


829 A.2d 1214; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 517


May 2, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
July 17, 2003, Decided  
July 17, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 1736 May Term 2002. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Judge CARRAFIELLO.
Purple Orchid, Inc. v. Pa. State Police, Bureau of Liquor Control Enforcement, 572 Pa. 171, 813 A.2d 801, 2002 Pa. LEXIS 3135 (Pa., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar was issued a summons for violating Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-493(10) by permitting lewd, immoral or improper entertainment on its premises. The bar challenged the citation at a hearing before an administrative law judge (ALJ). The ALJ upheld the citation, and the decision was affirmed by the Pennsylvania Liquor Control Board. The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) affirmed the citation. The bar appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the bar raised several issues. The appellate court found that the Commonwealth's prohibition of topless dancing in establishments that served alcohol did not violate the freedom of expression guaranteed by Pa. Const. art. 1, § 7. The Liquor Control Board (LCB) issued licenses to dispense alcohol on the condition that the license holder not permit lewd, immoral or improper entertainment. The LCB had the authority to impose this condition and topless dancing performed in licensed establishments could be lewd, immoral or improper entertainment per se. In addition, the creation of appellee Bureau of Liquor Control Enforcement by the legislature's 1987 revision to the Liquor Code did not deny due process to the bar because the operators of the bar acted with full knowledge that the behavior they allowed on their premises, and which the police officers observed, was lewd, immoral or improper behavior as a matter of law. Finally, the appellate court concluded that there was sufficient, competent evidence to support the trial court's conclusion that the behavior about which the officers testified constituted a violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-493(10).


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1989 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Piatek v. Pulaski Twp.


No. 604 C.D. 2002, No. 605 C.D. 2002, No. 606 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


828 A.2d 1164; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 499


October 7, 2002, Argued  
July 9, 2003, Decided  
July 9, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Piatek v. Pulaski Twp., 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1833 (Pa., Aug. 11, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 70068, 70069 & 70070 of 2001 M.D. Common Pleas Court of the County of Lawrence. Judge MOTTO.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult entertainment facility (AEF) owner sought review of a judgment of the Lawrence County, Pennsylvania, Court of Common Pleas, which affirmed the decision of the Pulaski Township Board of Supervisors (Board) denying applications AEF owner and employee licenses.


OVERVIEW: The township enacted an ordinance, which, inter alia, required the licensing of employees and operators of sexually oriented businesses. Existing adult businesses were given a 180-day grace period to apply for a license. Because the owner's business fell within the grace period. The owner did not apply for a license. Following the elapse of the grace period, township officials filed an injunction to preclude continued operations. In response, the owner challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance. The appellate court did not find the provisions of the ordinance to be content-based. The findings section of the ordinance clearly noted that its primary purpose was to address the secondary effects arising from the operation of an AEF business. Several of the legislative findings raised concerns relating to hours of operation of the facility. The appellate court held that the limitation of hours was no greater than was necessary to accomplish legitimate governmental goals. As an AEF in operation at the time of the ordinance's enactment, the business had ample opportunity to pursue declaratory relief to determine the constitutionality of the ordinance. It did not do so.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court was affirmed.

 

1990 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Koken v. Legion Ins. Co.


No. 183 M.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


831 A.2d 1196; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 621



June 26, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Koken v. Legion Ins. Co., 865 A.2d 1, 2004 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 974 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2004)
Later proceeding at Koken v. Legion Ins. Co., 865 A.2d 945, 2004 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 975 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2004)
Affirmed by Koken v. Villanova Ins. Co., 583 Pa. 400, 878 A.2d 51, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1479 (2005)
Related proceeding at Miss. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. MS Cas. Ins. Co., 947 So. 2d 865, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 622 (Miss., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Court granted Rehabilitator's petition to terminate rehabilitation and set conditions and filing date for Rehabilitator's proposed order of liquidation. Court also granted motions of third-party beneficiaries for direct access to reinsurance agreements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Pennsylvania Insurance Commissioner, in her capacity as the rehabilitator of two insurers, filed petitions seeking the liquidation of respondent insurers on the grounds that the insurers consented to the liquidation, they were insolvent, further rehabilitation was futile and could increase the risk of loss to creditors and others, and there was a need to trigger state guaranty funds. Various parties intervened.


OVERVIEW: The insurers were basically fronting companies that issued insurance policies that were largely reinsured by other insurers. Various parties, including the controlling shareholder of both insurers and various policyholders, were granted intervention in the action to state their position with respect to the potential liquidation. The positions were assorted, but many opposed the relief requested by the rehabilitator, noting that it would create hardship for their own clients, that they would prefer direct access to the reinsurance, that the state guaranty funds would be inadequate, and that rehabilitation was feasible. After careful consideration by the court of all parties' positions, it held that the rehabilitator had no authority to purportedly consent on the insurers' behalf to the liquidation, pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 40, § 221.18(a). The court found that liquidation was inevitable because rehabilitation would substantially increase the risk of loss, but that allowing direct access to the reinsurers was mandated in order to protect policyholder interests. It was noted that the policyholders had established third-party beneficiary rights under the reinsurance agreements.


OUTCOME: The court granted the rehabilitator's petition to terminate the rehabilitation, and granted direct access to the reinsurance agreements to those intervenors which demonstrated third-party beneficiary status. The court directed the rehabilitator to draft plans as to the direct access, as well as to the liquidation of the insurer, which was also granted.

 

1991 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Tobin


No. 2205 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


828 A.2d 415; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 453


April 2, 2003, Argued  
June 25, 2003, Decided  
June 25, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. Tobin, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2307 (Pa., Dec. 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 1569-02 Common Pleas Court of the County of Schuylkill. Judge RUBRIGHT, S.J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Schuylkill County (Pennsylvania), which found him guilty of violating City of Pottsville, Pa., Ordinance § 176 and directed that he pay fines and restitution.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that (1) the ordinance, which he asserted criminalized a landlord's refusal to permit warrantless entry, was unconstitutional; (2) the fee charged for inspections was actually an invalid tax; and (3) the ordinance violated equal protection. The main issue was whether defendant could be criminally convicted for refusing to allow a code enforcement inspector access to the residential apartments he owned and leased in the absence of a search warrant. The city argued that a warrant was not required because the search involved an industry that was "pervasively" regulated. The appellate court concluded that an administrative warrant had to be obtained prior to convicting an owner for failing to permit access to conduct inspections under the ordinance. Because no warrant was issued, defendant's conviction violated his Fourth Amendment right to be free from unreasonable warrantless searches. However, defendant failed to show an unconstitutional tax because there was no evidence that the fee was for revenue-raising purposes, rather than to defer administrative enforcement costs. Also, there was a rational basis for the inspection of leased residential premises.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was reversed.

Mitchell v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 2131 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


826 A.2d 936; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 448


February 21, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
June 23, 2003, Decided  
June 23, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 834 of 2002. Westmoreland. MARKER.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his statutory appeal from a one-year suspension of his operating privileges imposed by appellee Department of Transportation, Bureau of Driver Licensing.


OVERVIEW: An off-duty police officer in an unmarked car noticed a car behind him swerving and driving erratically. The officer put a red light on his car and pulled over the licensee's vehicle, at which time he identified himself as an officer. The officer testified that the driver appeared intoxicated and he failed a field sobriety test, and accordingly, the officer arrested the licensee and transported him to the hospital for a blood test. However, the licensee refused the test, despite having been informed of the consequences of such refusal. The Department sent the licensee a notice that his operating privileges were being suspended for one year, pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1546(b)(1), for his refusal to submit to the testing. The licensee's appeal resulted in a hearing, whereupon the trial court determined that the suspension was proper because the officer had reasonable grounds to suspect that the licensee was operating the vehicle in an intoxicated state. The licensee sought further review and the court held that the validity of the arrest was irrelevant for determining whether suspension was proper for the licensee's refusal to submit to a chemical test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

North-Central Pa. Trial Lawyers Ass'n v. Weaver


No. 869 M.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


827 A.2d 550; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 437


April 1, 2003, Argued  
June 18, 2003, Decided  
June 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 26, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Preliminary objections overruled in part and sustained in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the Commonwealth, filed preliminary objections to a complaint filed by petitioners, a trial lawyers association and an attorney, seeking a declaration that 2002 Pa. Laws 127 (Act 127), relating in part to venue in medical professional liability actions, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondents argued that the association lacked standing to bring the suit and that petitioners failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The court concluded that petitioners had standing to maintain the action because the petition for review alleged that a number of the association's members were members in good standing of the bar of Pennsylvania who engaged in medical malpractice litigation and who would be directly and substantially affected by the changes in the venue rules contained in Act 127 and whose clients would be directly and substantially affected. In addition, the court agreed with petitioners that venue in civil cases concerned a matter of pure procedure. In the absence of a countervailing constitutional provision authorizing the legislature to act in regard to venue in a particular area, the matter was committed to the exclusive authority of the Pennsylvania Supreme Court under Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(c). Thus, the court concluded that Act 127, insofar as it purported to alter the rules relating to venue in regard to medical professional liability actions generally, exceeded the authority of the legislature and was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The preliminary objection of respondents raising a question of standing was overruled. The preliminary objections of respondents asserting failure to state a cause of action under the constitutional provision relating to the passage of laws were sustained. The preliminary objection of respondents asserting failure to state cause of action under the constitutional rules regarding venue was overruled.

 

1994 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


N. Tier Solid Waste Auth. v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 876 M.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


825 A.2d 793; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 387


April 1, 2003, Argued  
June 6, 2003, Decided  
June 6, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part N. Tier Solid Waste Auth. v. Commonwealth, 2004 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 807 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Nov. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.



DISPOSITION: Respondents' preliminary objections in nature of demurrers overruled. Respondents shall file answers.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, its Department of Revenue and its Secretary, and its Department of Environmental Protection and its Secretary (collectively, the Commonwealth), filed preliminary objections in the nature of demurrers in the trial court (Pennsylvania), in an action filed by petitioners, three municipal solid waste authorities, challenging the solid waste disposal fee authorized in 2002 Pa. Laws 90, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth argued that the Pennsylvania Municipalities Authorities Act, 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. 5601 et seq., did not apply to a disposal fee on municipal waste. The appellate court held that insofar as the acceptance and proper disposal of waste enhanced the health and living conditions of Pennsylvania citizens, the authorities stated a claim for statutory tax exemption for things used in that function. Pennsylvania law was clear that property acquired or used by an authority did not lose its tax exemption unless a statute clearly and unequivocally expressed the legislative will that such property was not immune. For the purpose of resolving the preliminary objections, the authorities stated a claim for statutory exemption from taxation on things used by them to improve the living conditions of Pennsylvania citizens. Respondents failed to show a clear intent on the part of the legislature to overcome the statutory exemption. The authorities claim that the fee violated their state and federal constitution rights to unimpaired contracts stated a claim, as they alleged that the fee could not be passed on to all of their customers.


OUTCOME: The preliminary objections were overruled.

 

1995 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Grossman v. State Bd. of Psychology


No. 3023 C.D. 2001


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


825 A.2d 748; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 379


January 17, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
June 2, 2003, Decided  
June 2, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Grossman v. State Bd. of Psychology, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2139 (Pa., Nov. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 0093-63-00. State Agency, State Board of Psychology.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent psychologist petitioned for review of an order of the Pennsylvania State Board of Psychology, which reprimanded him and assessed a civil penalty against him, in connection with his evaluation of a child and his testimony at a child custody hearing, after petitioner Pennsylvania Bureau of Professional and Occupational Affairs's motion to limit the psychologist's witnesses was granted.


OVERVIEW: The psychologist argued that the Board failed to provide proper notice of its interpretation of the American Psychological Association (APA) Guidelines. The appellate court found that although the APA ethical rules were framed as aspirations, they had been made mandatory by their inclusion in the Board's requirements for licensees. The Board properly held that the psychologist had violated the father's right to participate in major decisions as to his child by evaluating her without the father's consent and in continuing contact after being told to stop. The psychologist's argument that his conduct fell under the child abuse exception to the rule was rejected. The exclusion of a former Board member's testimony was proper, as previous Board policy was irrelevant. The Board's decision that the psychologist performed a custody evaluation was supported by the evidence. The psychologist's argument that the father's consent was not required because he was a litigant was rejected. However, the Board's determination that the psychologist acted unprofessionally was reversed, as the psychologist did not receive adequate notice that his testimony in the custody hearing was at issue.


OUTCOME: The reprimand of the psychologist was affirmed as to the violation of the ethical regulations count, but was reversed as to the unprofessional conduct count.

 

1996 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


McCrady v. Bd. of Prop. Assessment, Appeals, Review & Registry


No. 1750 C.D. 2002, No. 1751 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


827 A.2d 522; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 360


February 5, 2003, Argued  
May 20, 2003, Decided  
May 20, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended May 29, 2003. Application for reargument denied July 11, 2003.
Appeal denied by McCrady v. Bd. of Prop. Assessment, 577 Pa. 691, 844 A.2d 554, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 215 (Pa., Feb. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From Nos. GD 96-12415 & GD 99-9708. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Judge JAMES.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Allegheny Valley School District appealed the order of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) holding that appellee Allegheny County Board of Property Assessment, Appeals, and Review and Registry properly increased an assessment of appellee owner's property to include a value for a trailer added to the land, but it reversed the Board's assessment of the land underlying the trailer as an improper spot assessment.


OVERVIEW: The unimproved land at issue was leased by the owner to the tenant. The tenant moved a trailer onto the property. The county assessor learned of the existence of the trailer on the property in 1995 and that it had been on the property since at least 1991. The assessor increased the 1996 assessment of the land from $ 2,400 to $ 61,500. The assessor used a market value approach, relying upon the sale of land across the street from the owner's property to determine the value of the owner's land. The assessor then assessed the trailer on the property, which was found to be $ 5,000. The assessment of the property for 1991 through 1995 was retroactively increased. The owner asserted that the reassessment of land from 1991 through 1996 constituted an impermissible spot assessment. The assessor's actions of assigning a new valuation for the land and trailer altered the physical facts of the property's assessment and its valuation, which constituted a new assessment of the property that could only be done on a countywide basis. Thus, the Board had no authority under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 5452.13 to reassess the property beyond the change produced by the addition of the trailer.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1997 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re Condemnation (Appeal of New Garden Theatre)


No. 65 C.D. 1999, No. 1063 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


823 A.2d 1086; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 359


February 4, 2003, Argued  
May 19, 2003, Decided  
May 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, Motion dismissed by In re Condemnation by Urban Redevelopment Auth., 577 Pa. 703, 847 A.2d 59, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 634 (2004)
Affirmed by In re Condemnation By Urban Redevelopment Auth. of Pittsburgh, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 2513 (Pa., Dec. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. GD 97-7170. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Judge PENKOWER.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an adult theatre and a realty company, appealed from two orders by the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) in an eminent domain case dismissing and overruling the preliminary objections of the theatre and the realty company to the declaration of taking filed by respondent, an urban redevelopment authority.


OVERVIEW: The theatre alleged that it was improperly barred from filing objections to the taking. The appellate court held that the theatre's duty to file timely objections was triggered by actual notice to a related party. The authority had a generally applicable power to combat blight and to promote economic redevelopment. The authority's exercise of its eminent domain power to combat blight did not transform the taking into a time, place, and manner restriction on free speech. The only direct evidence of the authority's view of the use of the property as an adult theatre was its acknowledgement that there was a perception that the adult theatre was part of the negative image of the area and was a factor in the decision not to permit new adult uses in the redevelopment plan. The authority's action was not subject to strict scrutiny as a content-based restriction on First Amendment rights. The intermediate scrutiny test was met. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to analyze independently the claims under Pa. Const. art. I, § 7. Even if a least intrusive means test was applied, the least restrictive means for accomplishing a legitimate governmental interest was employed.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

1998 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


DeWeese v. Weaver


No. 567 M.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


824 A.2d 364; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 396


December 4, 2002, Argued  
May 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by DeWeese v. Weaver, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 407 (Pa. Commw. Ct., July 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. ORIGINAL JURISDICTION



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Respondent's preliminary objections to petition for review overruled in part and sustained in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner representatives filed a petition for review to have amendments to the Pennsylvania Judicial Code declared unconstitutional under the single subject rule and related provisions of the Pennsylvania Constitution and to have enforcement of the statutory amendments enjoined. Respondent Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania filed preliminary objections asserting that the petition for review failed to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: In the process of amending Pennsylvania DNA Detection of Sexual and Violent Offenders Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 7651 et seq., the Pennsylvania House of Representatives gave the bill a new title. It provided that the bill amended the Pennsylvania Judicial Code and that the bill provided, in part, for DNA testing for certain offenders and for the apportionment of liability and damages in negligence actions. The title of the bill remained when it was passed. The representatives asserted that the amended act, 2002 Pa. Laws 57, violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 1, 3. The appellate court found that the representatives stated a claim under Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, which prohibited passage of bills containing more than one subject. Requiring DNA samples from felony sex offenders did not relate to joint and several liability. Also, the expungement of a DNA record under 2002 Pa. Laws 57 did not relate to the main purpose of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4701 et seq. The representatives failed to state a claim under Pa. Const. art. III, § 1, which prohibited deceptive titles, as they did not allege that the title was so unclear as to be fraudulent or deceptive.


OUTCOME: The Secretary's preliminary objections were overruled with regard to the claim that the bill at issue violated the single subject rule of the Pennsylvania Constitution, but the preliminary objections were sustained with regard to the claim that the bill at issue violated the constitutional provision prohibiting deceptive titles.

 

1999 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Sturpe v. Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review


No. 1779 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


823 A.2d 239; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 283; 25 A.L.R.6th 635; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P12,433


March 5, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
May 5, 2003, Decided  
May 5, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. B-401571. State Agency Unemployment Compensation Board of Review.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a worker, sought review of an order of respondent, the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, which denied the worker unemployment compensation benefits under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 802(b).


OVERVIEW: The worker resigned from her job after her husband was transferred to Ohio as part of his employment. Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, § 802(b), provided that an employee was ineligible for benefits when her unemployment was the result of her voluntarily terminating her employment without a necessitous and compelling reason. The necessitous and compelling reason requirement referred to real and substantial circumstances that forced the employee to terminate employment and that would compel a reasonable person under those circumstances to act in the same manner. The court found that the worker and her husband had maintained separate living arrangements for some time prior to the worker's resignation. The court held that the worker offered no evidence of economic hardship in maintaining separate living arrangements or that her move to Ohio caused insurmountable commuting problems. The commuting problems alleged in the present case involved a more onerous commute to spend weekends together, and these commuting problems did not give rise to an award of benefits. The court held that the worker's resignation was based on a personal preference and a desire to maintain the family unit.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

2000 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Wert v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 1590 C.D. 2002


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


821 A.2d 182; 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 245


February 7, 2003, Argued  
April 14, 2003, Decided  
April 14, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 2001-7540-27-6. Common Pleas Court of the County of Bucks. Judge CLARK, S.J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of an order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Bucks (Pennsylvania), which sustained a one-year suspension of his driver's license by appellee, the Department of Transportation, Bureau of Driver Licensing, under the Driver's License Compact, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1581-1586, after the licensee was convicted of driving while intoxicated (DWI) in New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was arrested and convicted in New Jersey for DWI, after which the Department suspended his driver's license. On appeal, the licensee argued that his citizenship privileges and immunities and other constitutional rights had been violated. The court held that the Compact did not impose penalties for driving under the influence convictions on the basis of state citizenship because it enforced, without discrimination, the same rule. Thus, there was no disparate treatment by either New Jersey or Pennsylvania and the U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2 privileges and immunities claim failed. Nor was there any merit to the licensee's claim that his fundamental right to travel were abrogated because that right did not include the right to be excused from another state's highway laws and the licensee merely made bald assertions that he was treated more harshly than New Jersey drivers who were convicted of DWI. Similarly, the licensee's claim of disparate treatment of Pennsylvanians was an equal protection claim that had been rejected by the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania. Finally, the licensee's claims under the Pennsylvania Constitution were not presented adequately to merit review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.
